Abu Hanifa on Discussing the Companions
Abu Hanifa advises restraint and explains necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hanifa's nuanced position that while refraining from discussing the Companions' conflicts is safer, necessity can justify explanation.

Core Idea
Refraining is safer, but necessity can require mention.

This passage presents Abu Hanifa's reasoning on how to approach the historical events involving the Companions. While he emphasizes that silence is safer, he acknowledges that scholars had to record these events to protect hearts from false beliefs. Let's explore his balanced view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of Abu Hanifa's argument.
Notice the conditional structure: 'لولا علي...' and the shift to 'إلا أن الحالة...'
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's main statement
Find where Abu Hanifa says that refraining is safer and closer to the Prophet's command. Note the hadith 'If my Companions are mentioned, then refrain.'
3
Understand the exception
Notice the clause 'إلا أن الحالة التي بيناها دعتنا إلى ذكر أحوالهم' which explains why scholars did record these events. Consider why this exception exists.
The reason is to safeguard hearts from false beliefs.
4
See how necessity operated
The passage explains that the jurists and theologians undertook the mention to protect hearts, and that Ali's example provided guidance. Reflect on how this principle balances caution and clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وترك اغتنام أموالهم، وغير ذلك من الأحكام التي أخذها فقهاء الأمة عن معاملة عليه وسيرته فيهم حتى قال أبو حنيفة – قدس الله روحه -: "لولا علي ه لم نكن نعرف السيرة في الخوارج لكان الكف عن ذكر أحوالهم والإغضاء عما جرى بينهم ودفع أحوالهم جملةً عن القلوب والألسن أسلم في الدين وأوفق بما مَنَّ الله علينا في تأخير انتسابنا عن الوقف الذي فيه خوف الاشتراك فيما لا يحل في الدين، والميل إلى ما الحق في غيره، وأقرب إلى ما دل عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: "إذا ذكر أصحابي فأمسكوا" وفي الخوض في أحوالهم مع إمساك اللسان انتشار القلوب لأن القلوب لا تمتنع عن فعلها وذلك أشد من الألسن، إلا أن الحالة التي بيناها دعتنا إلى ذكر أحوالهم والإخبار عما جرى بينهم، فقام حفاظ الأمة بذكرها والمتكلمون بالكشف عن وجوه ذلك، صيانةً للقلوب عن اعتقاد ما لا يحل فيهم مع ما أكرمهم الله تعالى به من صحبة النبي، ونصرة دينه، ونقل شريعته، وتبليغ وحيه، ثم إن فقهاء الأمة أخذوا ذلك عن معاملة علي، ثم يجوز أن يكون ذلك قد عرف النبي عليه السلام غيره لكنهم لم يخرجوا إلى وقت علي، ورأوا بالذي فعله هو الله كفاية إذ لم يغيروا عليه، وكان فعله ظاهراً بحيث عرفه الكل، وبلغ مبلغا لو ظهر منه منكر ليلزم التغيير، ويجوز أن يكون خصه النبي عليه السلام بتعليم الأحكام بما قد علم أنه يخص بالحاجة إلى ذلك، وفي قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إِنَّا نقاتل على التنزيل وأنت تقاتل على التأويل" دليل أن جميع ما فعل فعل عن علم وعلى موافقة الشريعة، والله أعلم.
ثم في جميع ما جرى من علي وأتباعه من المعاملة مع مخالفيهم والامتناع عن أن يعاملوهم معاملة الكفار أو المرتدين بل قال : إخواننا بغوا علينا – وقوله لابن طلحة - أنا وأبوك من أهل هذه الآية (وَنَزَعْنَا مَا فِي صُدُورِهِم مِّنْ غِلٍّ) دلالة بغض قول المعتزلة والخوارج، والله الموفق.
And abandoning the taking of their wealth, and other rulings which the jurists of the community took from the treatment of Ali and his conduct towards them, until Abu Hanifa – may Allah sanctify his soul – said: "Were it not for Ali, we would not know the conduct regarding the Khawarij; indeed, refraining from mentioning their states and overlooking what occurred among them, and removing their states altogether from hearts and tongues, is safer in religion and more consistent with what Allah has bestowed upon us in delaying our affiliation from the situation where there is fear of sharing in what is not permissible in religion, and inclining to what is correct in other than it, and closer to what the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, indicated by his saying: 'When my Companions are mentioned, then refrain.' And in delving into their states while restraining the tongue, the hearts become agitated because the hearts do not refrain from their action, and that is more severe than tongues. However, the situation we have described necessitated that we mention their states and inform about what occurred among them. So the preservers of the community undertook their mention, and the theologians uncovered the aspects of that, as a safeguard for hearts from believing what is not permissible concerning them, along with what Allah Almighty honored them with of companionship of the Prophet, supporting His religion, conveying His law, and delivering His revelation. Then the jurists of the community took that from the treatment of Ali. Then it is possible that the Prophet, peace be upon him, knew other than him but they did not go beyond until the time of Ali, and they saw that what he did was sufficient for Allah since they did not change it, and his action was apparent such that everyone knew it, and it reached a level that if a reprehensible act had appeared from him, change would have been obligatory. And it is possible that the Prophet, peace be upon him, singled him out for teaching the rulings because it was known that he would be singled out for the need for that. And in his saying, peace be upon him: 'We fight over the revelation and you fight over the interpretation,' there is evidence that all that he did was done with knowledge and in accordance with the law. And Allah knows best. Then, in all that occurred from Ali and his followers of treatment with their opponents and refraining from treating them as they treat disbelievers or apostates, rather he said: 'Our brothers have rebelled against us' – and his saying to Ibn Talha: 'I and your father are among the people of this verse: “And We shall remove from their breasts any rancor”' – there is an indication of the repudiation of the saying of the Mu'tazila and the Khawarij. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1180

Commentary
This passage discusses the proper attitude towards the conflicts that occurred among the Companions, particularly concerning Ali and the Khawarij. The author begins by stating that the jurists derived rulings from Ali's treatment of the Khawarij. Then he quotes Abu Hanifa, who expresses that refraining from discussing these events would be safer, but necessity forced scholars to record them to protect hearts from false beliefs. Abu Hanifa notes that Ali's actions were consistent with the Prophet's teachings, evidenced by the hadith 'We fight over the revelation and you fight over the interpretation.' The author then explains that Ali did not treat his opponents as disbelievers or apostates, calling them 'our brothers who have rebelled against us,' and citing the verse about removing rancor, which refutes the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. The passage concludes by affirming Allah's guidance.

Key Terms
أصحابي
السيرة
الخوارج
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is always forbidden to discuss conflicts among the Companions.
Correction: Abu Hanifa shows that while refraining is safer, necessity can justify mention to protect correct belief.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the default ruling regarding mentioning the states of the Companions?
A) It is absolutely forbidden
B) It is always obligatory
C) Refraining is safer, but necessity can justify it
D) Only Ali himself should mention them

Key Takeaway
While silence is safer, scholars may address events among the Companions if needed to protect correct beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across discussions about the Companions' conflicts, do you feel a pull to engage in idle talk? In light of Abu Hanifa's warning, what will you do the next time such a conversation arises?
?
Have you ever judged a Companion based on reports you heard without proper context? This lesson shows that scholars only discussed these events to protect hearts from false beliefs. Is your own heart safe from misconceptions? What is one step you will take to ensure you hold a correct view of all the Sahabah?
?
The passage says that refraining is safer, but necessity compelled scholars to act. Are you using 'necessity' as an excuse to indulge in unnecessary talk, or are you genuinely seeking to protect your faith? Make a concrete commitment to only speak about the Companions with the reverence and purpose demonstrated here.

Ali's Treatment of His Opponents
Ali's conduct refutes extremist sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's conduct towards his opponents refutes the claims of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij that they should be treated as disbelievers.

Core Idea
Ali called his opponents 'brothers,' showing they were not disbelievers.

The passage now turns to Ali's own example. By not treating those who fought him as apostates or disbelievers, Ali demonstrated the correct Islamic stance. This directly refutes the extremist positions of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. Let's examine his words and the Quranic verse he cited.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on Ali's statement and the Quranic verse he quoted.
The verse is about removing rancor from hearts.
2
Identify Ali's treatment of his opponents
Notice that Ali refrained from treating his opponents as disbelievers or apostates. Instead, he called them 'our brothers who have rebelled against us.'
This is a key point of differentiation from the Khawarij.
3
Understand the refutation
The author states that this conduct and Ali's quoting of the verse indicate repudiation of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. Reflect on why their positions are refuted by Ali's example.
The Mu'tazila and Khawarij held that major sinners are not believers, but Ali's actions show otherwise.

?

?

?
Ali included his opponent in a verse about Paradise. Is there anyone you have deemed unworthy of Paradise due to their actions against you? Will you repent from that judgment and ask Allah to forgive them as you hope He forgives you?

Sects and Disagreements

6 min
The Wisdom of Ali's Arbitration and Refutation of the Khawarij
Defense of Ali's arbitration based on the unifying purpose of imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni scholars defended Ali's arbitration as a means of unification, and how the wisdom of imamate prioritizes unity over strict legal action.

Core Idea
Ali's arbitration was not a mistake but a wise application of imamate's unifying purpose.

The Khawarij accused Ali of error and disbelief for accepting arbitration instead of fighting. In this passage, the author explains that their view stems from ignorance of the imamate's true wisdom: to unite hearts. The passage shows that even war is only permitted as a last resort for reunification, and that the Quran itself prioritizes unification over strict legal application.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow before interpreting.
Notice the verse is cut off; focus on the logic.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Find where the author states the Sunni position and the Khawarij claim. Note the difference: correctness vs. error/disbelief.
The Khawarij insisted on fighting until submission.
3
Examine the author's refutation
The author attributes the Khawarij view to ignorance of imamate's wisdom. Understand how the wisdom is explained: unification of hearts as the cause of security and survival.
War is only a last resort after other means fail.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
The author quotes part of a verse about uniting hearts. Consider how this verse supports the argument that unification is a great blessing, overriding strict fighting obligation.
Think about how the verse is used as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في التحكيم فذهب أصحابنا وجميع أهل السنة إلى أن عليا كان مصيبًا في التحكيم، وزعمت الخوارج أنه كان مخطئًا فيه وقد كفر، إذ كان الواجب من أهل البغي هو المحاربة على ما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَإِنْ بَغَتْ إِحْدَتهُمَا عَلَى الْأُخْرَىٰ فَقَتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِيءَ إِلَى أَمْرِ الله ﴾ الآية، ولكن أصحابنا – رحمهم الله – قالوا: إن هذا قول من جهل حكمة الإمامة وعظم منزلتهما في أمر الدين والسياسة، فإن حكمة الإمامة إنما جلت ومنزلتها عظمت بما فيها من تألف الخلق واجتماع القلوب اللذين هما سبب الأمن والبقاء، وبهما الوفاء في كل مرتضى من الأفعال والأقوال، والبلوغ إلى كل مرتقى من الفضائل والآداب، وجعلت الحروب للتألف بُعد عن إصابته بسائر أسباب التألف من المحاجات وأنواع البر. ولذلك – والله أعلم – أخر الله فرض الجهاد والقتال عن سائر أنواع الفرائض حتى ينتهي أسباب التأليف والتفريق لها ثم تظهر المكابرات للعقول، والمعاندات للحق، وتزول منفعة المحاجة وأنواع البر واللطف فوضع القتال ليكون التألف بذلك، ولذلك عظم الله مننه على الخلق بتأليف القلوب فقال : ( وَأَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ لَوْ أَنفَقْتَ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا مَّا
As for the discussion regarding arbitration, our companions and all the Ahl al-Sunna hold that Ali was correct in the arbitration. The Khawarij claimed that he was mistaken in it and had disbelieved, since the obligation towards the rebellious party is to fight them, as Allah Almighty said: "But if one of them oppresses the other, then fight against the one that oppresses until it returns to the command of Allah" – the verse. However, our companions – may Allah have mercy on them – said: "This is the saying of one who is ignorant of the wisdom of the imamate and the greatness of their rank in matters of religion and politics. For the wisdom of the imamate is only magnified and its rank is great because of what it contains of bringing together creation and uniting hearts, which are the cause of security and survival, and through them fulfillment is achieved in every approved action and saying, and attainment of every high station of virtues and manners. And wars were made [as a means] for unification, far from missing it through other means of unification such as arguments and types of kindness. Therefore – and Allah knows best – Allah postponed the obligation of jihad and fighting behind all other types of obligations, until the causes of unification and division are exhausted, then the stubbornness of intellects and obstinacy against truth appear, and the benefit of argument and types of kindness and gentleness vanish, so fighting was placed so that unification would be through it. For that reason, Allah magnified His favors upon creation by uniting hearts, He said: 'And He united their hearts; if you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have united their hearts' – the verse.
Source pages p. 1181

Commentary
This passage defends Ali's decision to accept arbitration against the Khawarij. The author states that the Sunni position is that Ali was correct, while the Khawarij claimed he erred and disbelieved because they insisted on fighting until submission. The author refutes this by explaining that the Khawarij's view comes from ignorance of the wisdom of imamate, which prioritizes unification of hearts. The imamate's purpose is to bring people together, and even war is permitted only as a last resort for reunification, after other means like argument and kindness have failed. This is why jihad is postponed behind other obligations. The author cites the Quranic verse about uniting hearts to emphasize that unification is a great blessing from Allah, and it may override strict legal application in certain cases.

Key Terms
التحكيم
الخوارج
حكمة الإمامة
تألف القلوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's arbitration was a mistake because he should have continued fighting according to the Quranic command.
Correction: The Sunni scholars explain that arbitration was a means to unite hearts, which is the primary goal of imamate. War is only a last resort, and the command to fight is not absolute when unity can be achieved through other means.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the Sunni scholars defend Ali's arbitration?
A) Because Ali was forced to accept arbitration
B) Because arbitration was a means to unite hearts and preserve the community
C) Because the Khawarij were right about the need to fight
D) Because arbitration was the only option

Key Takeaway
The wisdom of imamate prioritizes unification of hearts, so Ali's arbitration was not a mistake but a means to achieve that unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when you insisted on being 'right' about a religious matter, even though it caused division with family or friends. Did your approach truly honor Allah’s command to unite hearts, or did it mirror the Khawarij’s error? What would Ali’s example require you to do differently if that situation arose again?
?
The Khawarij thought they were upholding the Quran by demanding war, yet they missed its deeper purpose. In your own life, is there a Quranic command or prophetic teaching you are using as a weapon to prove yourself superior rather than as a tool to bring hearts together? What is one step you can take today to prioritize unity over being right?
?
This lesson reveals that war is a last resort, only after argument and kindness fail. When you face conflict, do you exhaust all gentle means before resorting to harshness? Or do you jump to confrontation? Commit now: before your next disagreement, pause and ask, 'Is there a way to unite hearts here?' What will that look like in practice?

Defense of Ali's Arbitration: Wisdom of the Imamate
Defence of Ali's arbitration against Khawarij criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni scholars defend Ali's acceptance of arbitration as a wise act rooted in the higher purposes of the imamate, not a mistake or compromise.

Core Idea
The imamate's true purpose is reconciliation, not perpetual war.

The Khawarij condemned Ali for agreeing to arbitration at Siffin, citing a Qur'anic command to fight rebels. This passage presents the Sunni refutation, arguing that such criticism stems from ignorance of the imamate's deeper wisdom. The author explains that war is only a last resort; the ultimate goal is always to unite hearts and establish peace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overall sense of the argument. Notice the author's structure: stating the Khawarij position, then the Sunni response.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the argument is complete in meaning but the text is cut off.
2
Identify the Khawarij objection
What is the Khawarij's claim? They cite Qur'an 49:9 to argue that Ali should have fought Mu'awiya, not arbitrated. Why do they consider this a grave error?
3
Examine the refutation: wisdom of imamate
The author argues that the Khawarij are ignorant of the true purpose of the imamate: to bring about reconciliation and unity of hearts. Wars are only a means to that end when other methods fail.
Note the Qur'anic verses cited: 8:63 and 3:103.
4
Understand the precedents and final critique
The author gives examples from the Qur'an (spousal arbitration) and the Prophet's treaty of Hudaybiyya. Finally, he criticizes the Khawarij for inconsistency: they accepted Ali's imamate but reject his judgment.
This step ties together the entire argument.

وأما الكلام في التحكيم فذهب أصحابنا وجميع أهل السنة إلى أن عليا كان مصيبًا في التحكيم، وزعمت الخوارج أنه كان مخطئًا فيه وقد كفر، إذ كان الواجب من أهل البغي هو المحاربة على ما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَإِنْ بَغَتْ إِحْدَتهُمَا عَلَى الْأُخْرَىٰ فَقَتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِيءَ إِلَى أَمْرِ الله ﴾ (۳) الآية، ولكن أصحابنا – رحمهم الله – قالوا: إن هذا قول من جهل حكمة الإمامة وعظم منزلتهما في أمر الدين والسياسة، فإن حكمة الإمامة إنما جلت ومنزلتها عظمت بما فيها من تألف الخلق واجتماع القلوب اللذين هما سبب الأمن والبقاء، وبهما الوفاء في كل مرتضى من الأفعال والأقوال، والبلوغ إلى كل مرتقى من الفضائل والآداب، وجعلت (٤) الحروب للتألف بُعد عن إصابته بسائر أسباب التألف من المحاجات وأنواع البر. ولذلك – والله أعلم – أخر (الله) فرض الجهاد والقتال عن سائر أنواع الفرائض حتى ينتهي أسباب التأليف والتفريق لها ثم تظهر ) () المكابرات للعقول، والمعاندات للحق، وتزول منفعة المحاجة وأنواع البر واللطف فوضع القتال ليكون التألف بذلك، ولذلك عظم الله مننه على الخلق بتأليف القلوب فقال : ( وَأَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ لَوْ أَنفَقْتَ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا مَّا الْفَتَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ الله أَلف بينهم (۱) وقال : فَأَصْبَحْتُم بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانَا ) (٢) الآية أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فإذا كان التأليف موجودًا بدون الحرب وإراقة الدماء، وتغلب على ذلك الطمع بما يعرفه من سآمة الفريقين، وما يظهر من آثار طلب الراحة (۳) منهم، والظفر بالأمن كانت الحكمة في الاشتغال (٤) به لتندفع معرة القتال وتتألف القلوب وتتحد الكلمة، فعلي له لما عاين آثار السامة في القوم رجا أن يحصل تألف القلوب بالتحكيم، واشتغل به وهو الغاية من الحكمة والنهاية فى الشفقة والمرحمة على الأمة على رجاء منه أن يصيب من أسندت إليه الحكومة الحق ويظفر بالثواب، فيكون في ذلك البلوغ إلى ما جعلت له الحروب على المسالمة والمصالحة اقتداء بما أمر الله تعالى من نصب الحكمين في الاختلاف بين الزوجين وما نصب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الحكمين في اختلاف وقع بينه وبين أهل مكة، وما جرى من الاصطلاح، فالأمة التي جاءت فيهم الشهادة عن الله تعالى بالآخرة وأمر الدين الذي عظم أمره التدبر والنظر، والإمامة التي المقصود منها التأليف والأمن أحق أن يعمل لها ذلك، ثم هؤلاء لما أقروا بالإمامة والخلافة وعلموا بالأسباب التي ظهرت لهم من نفسه(۹) مما صلح بها للخلافة، ثم لم تكن تغيرت تلك في نفسه ولا تبدلت ثم كان التحكيم منه حكما حكم به بسبب الإمامة فيلزمهم بحق إمامته القبول منه وإن ضاق عليهم وجه معرفة عذره في ذلك، ثم العجب من غباوة الخوارج أنهم خطأوه في التحكيم، ولو أنهم جعلوا ذلك حجة لهم عليه فيما كان (٦) من قبل، إذ كيف لم يبدأ بالمصالحة ثم كان يرجع إلى الحروب كان أقرب من أن جعلوا الأمر الأول من الحروب دلالة على
As for the speech concerning arbitration, our companions and all the people of the Sunnah held that Ali was correct in the arbitration, and the Khawarij claimed that he was mistaken therein and had disbelieved, because the obligation concerning the people of transgression is to fight them according to what God Almighty said: 'Then if one of them transgresses against the other, fight the one that transgresses until it returns to the command of God' (3) the verse. But our companions – may God have mercy on them – said: This is a saying of one who is ignorant of the wisdom of the imamate and the greatness of their station in the matter of religion and politics. For the wisdom of the imamate is exalted and its station is magnified only by what is in it of reconciliation of creation and unification of hearts, which are the cause of security and survival, and by them is fulfillment in every approved action and speech, and attainment of every high rank of virtues and manners. And wars were made for reconciliation, far from achieving it through other means of reconciliation such as arguments and types of goodness. Therefore – and God knows best – God postponed the obligation of jihad and fighting over other types of obligations until the means of reconciliation and division for them are exhausted, then stubbornness against intellects and obstinacy against truth appear, and the benefit of argument and types of goodness and kindness cease, so fighting was placed so that reconciliation might be thereby. Therefore God magnified His favors upon creation by reconciling hearts, saying: 'And He reconciled between their hearts; if you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have reconciled between their hearts, but God reconciled between them' (1), and He said: 'So you became by His grace brothers' (2) the verse; He reconciled between them. So if reconciliation exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what is known of the weariness of the two parties, and what appears of the effects of seeking ease from them, and attaining security, then wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the shame of fighting and to reconcile hearts and unite the word. So Ali, when he saw the effects of weariness in the people, hoped that reconciliation of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he engaged in it, and it is the ultimate goal of wisdom and the extreme of compassion and mercy upon the community, hoping that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted would hit upon the truth and attain reward. So in that is the attainment of that for which wars were made for peace and reconciliation, following the example of what God Almighty commanded of appointing two arbiters in the disagreement between spouses, and what the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, appointed two arbiters in a disagreement that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what occurred of reconciliation. So the community which has been given testimony from God Almighty concerning the afterlife and the matter of religion whose affair – reflection and consideration – is greatly esteemed, and the imamate whose purpose is reconciliation and security, is more deserving that this be done for it. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and the caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his own self (9) by which he was fit for the caliphate, then those (reasons) had not changed in his self nor been altered, then the arbitration from him was a judgment he made due to the imamate, so it is incumbent upon them by the right of his imamate to accept it from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that is difficult for them. Then it is amazing at the stupidity of the Khawarij that they faulted him in the arbitration, and had they made that a proof against him concerning what was before, for why did he not begin with reconciliation and then return to war? That would have been closer than that they make the first matter of war an indication of...
Source pages p. 1181

Commentary
This passage is a theological-historical argument defending the position of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may God be pleased with him) regarding the arbitration (tahkim) at the Battle of Siffin, against the Khawarij who accused him of error and apostasy. The author begins by stating the consensus of the Sunni school (our companions and all people of the Sunnah) that Ali was correct in accepting arbitration, while the Khawarij falsely claimed he erred and thereby became a disbeliever. The Khawarij based their claim on the Qur'anic verse (49:9) which commands fighting the transgressing party until it returns to God's command, arguing that Ali should have continued fighting rather than resorting to arbitration.

The author then refutes this view by asserting that it stems from ignorance of the true wisdom of the imamate and the high station of both Ali and Mu'awiya in matters of religion and politics. The imamate is established primarily to bring about harmony among people (ta'lif al-khalq) and unity of hearts (ijtima' al-qulub), which are the foundations of security and survival. Wars, including those commanded in jihad, are ultimately meant to achieve reconciliation when other means fail. The author explains that God postponed the obligation of jihad until after other means of reconciliation—such as arguments (muhajjat) and acts of goodness—have been exhausted and become ineffective due to stubbornness. Only then is fighting prescribed as a last resort to bring about unity.

To support this, the author cites two Qur'anic verses: (8:63) where God says He reconciled the hearts of the believers, and (3:103) about becoming brothers by His grace. The point is that reconciliation can exist without war. Since the community was showing signs of war-weariness, Ali wisely sought arbitration to achieve peace, thereby fulfilling the ultimate purpose of war itself. The author emphasizes that Ali's action was the height of wisdom, compassion, and mercy toward the ummah, hoping that the appointed arbiters would reach the truth.

The author then provides precedents: the Qur'an commands appointing arbiters for marital disputes (4:35), and the Prophet himself appointed arbiters in the treaty of Hudaybiyya with the Meccans. If these are acceptable for personal and tribal disputes, then for the greater Muslim community—which bears witness to the afterlife and whose affairs require deliberation—the imamate's goal of unity and security makes arbitration even more appropriate.

Finally, the author criticizes the Khawarij for inconsistency: they acknowledged Ali's imamate and the reasons for his fitness for leadership, which had not changed. Since the arbitration was a judgment issued by virtue of his imamate, they are obliged to accept it. Moreover, if they fault him for arbitration, they should also fault him for not seeking reconciliation before the initial battles—which would be absurd. Thus their position is self-contradictory and based on ignorance.

Key Terms
التحكيم
الخوارج
الإمامة
التأليف
المحاجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's arbitration was a mistake that led to disunity and weakened Islam.
Correction: The author argues that arbitration was a wise act aimed at reconciliation, consistent with the higher purposes of the imamate and the ultimate goal of war itself.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the primary purpose of the imamate and of wars in Islam?
A) To dominate opponents through force
B) To achieve reconciliation and unity of hearts
C) To enforce a single political opinion
D) To establish a caliphate by any means

Key Takeaway
Ali's acceptance of arbitration was not a concession but a fulfillment of the imamate's purpose of achieving unity and peace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a current dispute in your life—whether with a family member, colleague, or fellow Muslim. Have you exhausted all means of reconciliation (kind words, patience, seeking mediation) before resorting to harshness or cutting ties? What would it look like to prioritize 'ta'lif' (unity of hearts) even if it means compromising your pride?
?
The Khawarij insisted on a literal command to fight, ignoring the deeper wisdom of the imamate. Where in your own life do you cling to rules or principles at the expense of the mercy and reconciliation that those rules are meant to serve? Will you ask Allah to soften your heart and make you a person of reconciliation?
?
When you see someone in authority making a decision you disagree with, do you immediately assume they are weak or wrong, as the Khawarij did with Ali? Or do you give them the benefit of the doubt, trusting their wisdom and knowledge? Make a commitment to seek understanding before judgment in your next disagreement.

4 min
The Priority of Peace in Islam
Establishing peace as the preferred outcome over war.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that in Islam peace and reconciliation are preferred over war, and that war is only a means to achieve peace.

Core Idea
Peace is the goal; war is only a means.

This lesson begins with a Quranic principle: Allah can unite hearts without war. The author then explains that when peace is possible, wisdom requires pursuing it to avoid bloodshed. This sets the foundation for understanding Ali's decision to accept arbitration.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic citation
Start by reading the Quranic verse cited: 'He brought together their hearts, but Allah brought them together' (Quran 8:63). Notice that it emphasizes divine unity without force.
2
Identify the core argument
The author argues that when peace can be achieved without war, it is wise to pursue it. Look for the phrase 'wisdom lies in engaging in it' and understand why.
3
Reflect on the goal of war
Consider the statement that the ultimate goal of war is peace and unification. This is a key principle in Islamic political thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ وَقَالَ فَأَصْبَحْتُمْ بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانًا الآيَةَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فَإِذَا كَانَ التَّأْلِيفُ مَوْجُودًا بِدُونِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِرَاقَةِ الدِّمَاءِ وَتَغَلَّبَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا يَعْرِفُهُ مِنْ سَآمَةِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ وَمَا يَظْهَرُ مِنْ آثَارِ طَلَبِ الرَّاحَةِ مِنْهُمْ وَالظَّفَرِ بِالْأَمْنِ كَانَتِ الْحِكْمَةُ فِي الِاشْتِغَالِ بِهِ لِتَنْدَفِعَ مَعَرَّةُ الْقِتَالِ وَتَتَأَلَّفَ الْقُلُوبُ وَتَتَّحِدَ الْكَلِمَةُ فَعَلِيٌّ لَمَّا عَايَنَ آثَارَ السَّامَةِ فِي الْقَوْمِ رَجَا أَنْ يَحْصُلَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ وَاشْتَغَلَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَايَةُ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالنِّهَايَةُ فِي الشَّفَقَةِ وَالْمَرْحَمَةِ عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ عَلَى رَجَاءٍ مِنْهُ أَنْ يُصِيبَ مَنْ أُسْنِدَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْحُكُومَةُ الْحَقَّ وَيَظْفَرَ بِالثَّوَابِ فَيَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْبُلُوغُ إِلَى مَا جُعِلَتْ لَهُ الْحُرُوبُ عَلَى الْمُسَالَمَةِ وَالْمُصَالَحَةِ اقْتِدَاءً بِمَا أَمَرَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَصْبِ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي الِاخْتِلَافِ بَيْنَ الزَّوْجَيْنِ وَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي اخْتِلَافٍ وَقَعَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَمَا جَرَى مِنَ الِاصْطِلَاحِ فَالْأُمَّةُ الَّتِي جَاءَتْ فِيهِمُ الشَّهَادَةُ عَنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِالْآخِرَةِ وَأَمْرُ الدِّينِ الَّذِي عَظُمَ أَمْرُهُ التَّدَبُّرُ وَالنَّظَرُ وَالْإِمَامَةُ الَّتِي الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهَا التَّأْلِيفُ وَالْأَمْنُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ يُعْمَلَ لَهَا ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ هَؤُلَاءِ لَمَّا أَقَرُّوا بِالْإِمَامَةِ وَالْخِلَافَةِ وَعَلِمُوا بِالْأَسْبَابِ الَّتِي ظَهَرَتْ لَهُمْ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ مِمَّا صَلَحَ بِهَا لِلْخِلَافَةِ ثُمَّ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَغَيَّرَتْ تِلْكَ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَبَدَّلَتْ ثُمَّ كَانَ التَّحْكِيمُ مِنْهُ حُكْمًا حَكَمَ بِهِ بِسَبَبِ الْإِمَامَةِ فَيَلْزَمُهُمْ بِحَقِّ إِمَامَتِهِ الْقَبُولُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ ضَاقَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَجْهُ مَعْرِفَةِ عُذْرِهِ فِي ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ الْعَجَبُ مِنْ غَبَاوَةِ الْخَوَارِجِ أَنَّهُمْ خَطَّأُوهُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا ذَلِكَ حُجَّةً لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ فِيمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَبْلُ إِذْ كَيْفَ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالْمُصَالَحَةِ ثُمَّ كَانَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْحُرُوبِ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ مِنْ أَنْ جَعَلُوا الْأَمْرَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنَ الْحُرُوبِ دَلَالَةً عَلَى خَطَئِهِ فِي الثَّانِي وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ فَاحِشَةٌ وَتَعَلُّقُهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي مُسْتَقِيمٌ لِأَنَّهُ ذُكِرَ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا وَنَحْنُ كَذَا نَقُولُ إِنَّ الِاشْتِغَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ أَوَّلًا بِالدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الصُّلْحِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِ الْيَأْسِ عَنِ الصُّلْحِ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْقِتَالِ لِيَحْصُلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِذَلِكَ وَهُوَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ وَاجْتِمَاعُ الْكَلِمَةِ وَاللَّهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ.
He brought together their hearts, but Allah brought them together, and He said: 'And you became, by His favor, brothers' the verse. He brought them together. So when unification exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what he knows of the weariness of the two parties and what appears of the effects of seeking rest from them and attaining security, wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the evil of fighting and to unite hearts and unify the word. So Ali, when he witnessed the effects of weariness among the people, hoped that unification of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he engaged in it, and it is the ultimate goal of wisdom and the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah, in hope that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted might attain the truth and gain reward. In that is the attainment of what wars are intended for: peace and reconciliation, following what Allah Almighty commanded in appointing two arbiters in dispute between spouses, and what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed two arbiters in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what took place of reconciliation. So the ummah, about whom testimony from Allah Almighty concerning the Hereafter came, and the matter of religion whose importance is deliberation and consideration, and the imamate whose purpose is unification and security, is more deserving that this be done for them. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his (Ali's) self that made him fit for the caliphate, and then those reasons did not change in him nor alter, and then the arbitration from him was a ruling he made due to the imamate, then it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that was narrow for them. Then the wonder is at the stupidity of the Khawarij that they considered him mistaken in the arbitration. Had they made that an argument against him concerning what happened before—why did he not begin with reconciliation and then resort to war?—that would be closer than their making the first matter of war an indication of his error in the second. This is gross ignorance. And their clinging to His statement: 'Then fight the one that transgresses' is valid, because it was mentioned after His statement: 'Then make peace between them.' And we likewise say: engagement should first be with invitation to peace, then after despair of peace, one returns to fighting to achieve the desired goal thereby, which is unification of hearts and unity of word. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1182

Commentary
This passage is a sustained defense of Ali's decision to accept arbitration (tahkim) at Siffin, refuting the Khawarij's charge that it was a sinful error. The author begins by citing Quranic verses showing that Allah can bring hearts together without war, establishing that peace is preferable. He then explains that Ali, seeing war-weariness, sought unification through arbitration as an act of wisdom and mercy. He draws parallels to Quranic arbitration between spouses and the Prophet's arbitration at Hudaybiyya. The author then argues that since the Khawarij accepted Ali's imamate, they must accept his judgment even if they don't fully understand his reasoning. He criticizes their inconsistency: they condemn arbitration but earlier accepted Ali's warfare. Finally, he clarifies the correct understanding of the Quranic command to fight the transgressor: it comes after the command to make peace, so priority is to invite to peace, and only when that fails to fight. The entire passage is structured as a systematic refutation of the Khawarij's position.

Key Terms
التأليف
الحكمة
القتال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary goal of engaging in arbitration or peace efforts?
A) To win the war quickly.
B) To avoid the evil of fighting and unite hearts.
C) To humiliate the enemy.
D) To gain more territory.

Key Takeaway
Peace is the preferred outcome in Islam; war is only a means to achieve it when necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a current conflict in your life—with a family member, friend, or colleague. Are you genuinely seeking peace, or are you more focused on being right or winning? What would it look like to prioritize peace over your own desires, and what is one concrete step you can take today to move toward reconciliation?
?
The author says wisdom lies in pursuing peace to 'repel the evil of fighting.' Is there any situation where you have allowed pride or anger to perpetuate conflict instead of seeking peace? What is that costing you, and are you willing to humble yourself to end it?
?
Allah can unite hearts without war, as the verse reminds us. When you face a difficult relationship, do you rely on your own efforts to force a resolution, or do you sincerely ask Allah to create unity? How can you increase your trust in Him to bring about peace in a seemingly hopeless situation?

6 min
The Wisdom of Ali's Arbitration
Defending Ali's arbitration as wise and following precedents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ali’s acceptance of arbitration was an act of wisdom and mercy, consistent with Quranic and Prophetic precedents.

Core Idea
Ali’s arbitration was the utmost wisdom and mercy for the ummah.

Having established that peace is preferred, the author now applies this principle to Ali’s situation at Siffin. He shows that Ali observed war-weariness and hoped for reconciliation, and that his decision follows the Quranic precedent of appointing arbiters and the Prophet’s example at Hudaybiyya.

Guided Path
1
Read about Ali's observation
Notice that Ali saw signs of weariness in both parties. This is the condition that makes peace-seeking wise, as per Lesson 1.
2
Identify the parallels
The author draws two parallels: Quranic arbitration between spouses and the Prophet's arbitration with the Quraysh at Hudaybiyya. See how these support Ali's action.
3
Summarize the argument
Ali’s arbitration was not a mistake but an act of compassion and hope for reconciliation, following divine and prophetic examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ وَقَالَ فَأَصْبَحْتُمْ بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانًا الآيَةَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فَإِذَا كَانَ التَّأْلِيفُ مَوْجُودًا بِدُونِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِرَاقَةِ الدِّمَاءِ وَتَغَلَّبَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا يَعْرِفُهُ مِنْ سَآمَةِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ وَمَا يَظْهَرُ مِنْ آثَارِ طَلَبِ الرَّاحَةِ مِنْهُمْ وَالظَّفَرِ بِالْأَمْنِ كَانَتِ الْحِكْمَةُ فِي الِاشْتِغَالِ بِهِ لِتَنْدَفِعَ مَعَرَّةُ الْقِتَالِ وَتَتَأَلَّفَ الْقُلُوبُ وَتَتَّحِدَ الْكَلِمَةُ فَعَلِيٌّ لَمَّا عَايَنَ آثَارَ السَّامَةِ فِي الْقَوْمِ رَجَا أَنْ يَحْصُلَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ وَاشْتَغَلَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَايَةُ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالنِّهَايَةُ فِي الشَّفَقَةِ وَالْمَرْحَمَةِ عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ عَلَى رَجَاءٍ مِنْهُ أَنْ يُصِيبَ مَنْ أُسْنِدَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْحُكُومَةُ الْحَقَّ وَيَظْفَرَ بِالثَّوَابِ فَيَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْبُلُوغُ إِلَى مَا جُعِلَتْ لَهُ الْحُرُوبُ عَلَى الْمُسَالَمَةِ وَالْمُصَالَحَةِ اقْتِدَاءً بِمَا أَمَرَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَصْبِ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي الِاخْتِلَافِ بَيْنَ الزَّوْجَيْنِ وَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي اخْتِلَافٍ وَقَعَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَمَا جَرَى مِنَ الِاصْطِلَاحِ فَالْأُمَّةُ الَّتِي جَاءَتْ فِيهِمُ الشَّهَادَةُ عَنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِالْآخِرَةِ وَأَمْرُ الدِّينِ الَّذِي عَظُمَ أَمْرُهُ التَّدَبُّرُ وَالنَّظَرُ وَالْإِمَامَةُ الَّتِي الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهَا التَّأْلِيفُ وَالْأَمْنُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ يُعْمَلَ لَهَا ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ هَؤُلَاءِ لَمَّا أَقَرُّوا بِالْإِمَامَةِ وَالْخِلَافَةِ وَعَلِمُوا بِالْأَسْبَابِ الَّتِي ظَهَرَتْ لَهُمْ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ مِمَّا صَلَحَ بِهَا لِلْخِلَافَةِ ثُمَّ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَغَيَّرَتْ تِلْكَ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَبَدَّلَتْ ثُمَّ كَانَ التَّحْكِيمُ مِنْهُ حُكْمًا حَكَمَ بِهِ بِسَبَبِ الْإِمَامَةِ فَيَلْزَمُهُمْ بِحَقِّ إِمَامَتِهِ الْقَبُولُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ ضَاقَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَجْهُ مَعْرِفَةِ عُذْرِهِ فِي ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ الْعَجَبُ مِنْ غَبَاوَةِ الْخَوَارِجِ أَنَّهُمْ خَطَّأُوهُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا ذَلِكَ حُجَّةً لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ فِيمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَبْلُ إِذْ كَيْفَ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالْمُصَالَحَةِ ثُمَّ كَانَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْحُرُوبِ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ مِنْ أَنْ جَعَلُوا الْأَمْرَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنَ الْحُرُوبِ دَلَالَةً عَلَى خَطَئِهِ فِي الثَّانِي وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ فَاحِشَةٌ وَتَعَلُّقُهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي مُسْتَقِيمٌ لِأَنَّهُ ذُكِرَ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا وَنَحْنُ كَذَا نَقُولُ إِنَّ الِاشْتِغَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ أَوَّلًا بِالدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الصُّلْحِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِ الْيَأْسِ عَنِ الصُّلْحِ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْقِتَالِ لِيَحْصُلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِذَلِكَ وَهُوَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ وَاجْتِمَاعُ الْكَلِمَةِ وَاللَّهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ.
He brought together their hearts, but Allah brought them together, and He said: 'And you became, by His favor, brothers' the verse. He brought them together. So when unification exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what he knows of the weariness of the two parties and what appears of the effects of seeking rest from them and attaining security, wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the evil of fighting and to unite hearts and unify the word. So Ali, when he witnessed the effects of weariness among the people, hoped that unification of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he engaged in it, and it is the ultimate goal of wisdom and the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah, in hope that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted might attain the truth and gain reward. In that is the attainment of what wars are intended for: peace and reconciliation, following what Allah Almighty commanded in appointing two arbiters in dispute between spouses, and what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed two arbiters in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what took place of reconciliation. So the ummah, about whom testimony from Allah Almighty concerning the Hereafter came, and the matter of religion whose importance is deliberation and consideration, and the imamate whose purpose is unification and security, is more deserving that this be done for them. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his (Ali's) self that made him fit for the caliphate, and then those reasons did not change in him nor alter, and then the arbitration from him was a ruling he made due to the imamate, then it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that was narrow for them. Then the wonder is at the stupidity of the Khawarij that they considered him mistaken in the arbitration. Had they made that an argument against him concerning what happened before—why did he not begin with reconciliation and then resort to war?—that would be closer than their making the first matter of war an indication of his error in the second. This is gross ignorance. And their clinging to His statement: 'Then fight the one that transgresses' is valid, because it was mentioned after His statement: 'Then make peace between them.' And we likewise say: engagement should first be with invitation to peace, then after despair of peace, one returns to fighting to achieve the desired goal thereby, which is unification of hearts and unity of word. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1182

Commentary
This passage is a sustained defense of Ali's decision to accept arbitration (tahkim) at Siffin, refuting the Khawarij's charge that it was a sinful error. The author begins by citing Quranic verses showing that Allah can bring hearts together without war, establishing that peace is preferable. He then explains that Ali, seeing war-weariness, sought unification through arbitration as an act of wisdom and mercy. He draws parallels to Quranic arbitration between spouses and the Prophet's arbitration at Hudaybiyya. The author then argues that since the Khawarij accepted Ali's imamate, they must accept his judgment even if they don't fully understand his reasoning. He criticizes their inconsistency: they condemn arbitration but earlier accepted Ali's warfare. Finally, he clarifies the correct understanding of the Quranic command to fight the transgressor: it comes after the command to make peace, so priority is to invite to peace, and only when that fails to fight. The entire passage is structured as a systematic refutation of the Khawarij's position.

Key Terms
التحكيم
السامة
الشفقة
المرحمة
الاقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Khawarij believed that any form of arbitration in conflict is a sin because it delays fighting the transgressor.
Correction: The author shows that arbitration is a prophetic practice and that Ali's action was in line with Quranic commands and the Prophet's example.

Checkpoint
Which two precedents does the author cite to support Ali's arbitration?
A) The arbitration at Hudaybiyya and the arbitration between two Muslim groups.
B) The Quranic command to appoint arbiters in marital disputes and the Prophet's arbitration at Hudaybiyya.
C) The arbitration of Abu Bakr and Umar.
D) The arbitration of the early caliphs.

Key Takeaway
Ali’s arbitration was not a mistake but a wise and compassionate act rooted in Quranic and Prophetic precedents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a heated disagreement, do you instinctively seek arbitration and peace, or do you insist on being right regardless of the cost? How does Ali's example of prioritizing unification of hearts challenge your default response? What specific step can you take this week to imitate his wisdom in a relationship where you've been stubborn?
?
The passage says Ali's action was 'the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah.' Think of a time when you chose a peaceful resolution over a confrontation. Was your motive truly compassion, or was it convenience or fear? How can you cultivate genuine mercy in your future conflicts, even when you feel you are in the right?
?
Ali followed the precedent of the Prophet's arbitration at Hudaybiyya. Reflect on a situation where you knew the sunnah but found it difficult to follow because it seemed weak or compromising. How does knowing that Ali — the lion of Allah — chose this path change your perception of strength? Are you willing to be seen as 'weak' for the sake of unity, as Ali was?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
8 min
Obedience to the Imam and Refuting the Khawarij
Refuting Khawarij arguments and establishing the correct sequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Khawarij were obligated to accept Ali's arbitration and the logical flaws in their objections, including the correct order of peace then fighting.

Core Idea
Accepting the imam's decision is obligatory; the Khawarij's critique is inconsistent and ignorant.

The author now turns to directly refute the Khawarij. He argues that since they acknowledged Ali as the rightful imam, they must accept his judgment even if they don't fully understand it. He then highlights their inconsistency: they condemned arbitration but had earlier accepted Ali's warfare. Finally, he clarifies the Quranic command to fight the transgressor, showing that peace must be sought first.

Guided Path
1
Understand the argument from imamate
The author says that because the Khawarij accepted Ali's imamate, they are bound by his decisions. This is a key principle of political obedience.
2
Recognize the inconsistency
The author points out that the Khawarij criticized Ali for arbitration after war, but if they had criticized him for not seeking peace first, that would be more logical. Instead, they made the earlier war a proof of error in the later peace.
3
Correct interpretation of the Quranic verse
The verse 'then fight the one that transgresses' (Quran 49:9) comes after 'then make peace between them', so the order is peace first, then fighting only if peace fails.

أَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ وَقَالَ فَأَصْبَحْتُمْ بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانًا الآيَةَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فَإِذَا كَانَ التَّأْلِيفُ مَوْجُودًا بِدُونِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِرَاقَةِ الدِّمَاءِ وَتَغَلَّبَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا يَعْرِفُهُ مِنْ سَآمَةِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ وَمَا يَظْهَرُ مِنْ آثَارِ طَلَبِ الرَّاحَةِ مِنْهُمْ وَالظَّفَرِ بِالْأَمْنِ كَانَتِ الْحِكْمَةُ فِي الِاشْتِغَالِ بِهِ لِتَنْدَفِعَ مَعَرَّةُ الْقِتَالِ وَتَتَأَلَّفَ الْقُلُوبُ وَتَتَّحِدَ الْكَلِمَةُ فَعَلِيٌّ لَمَّا عَايَنَ آثَارَ السَّامَةِ فِي الْقَوْمِ رَجَا أَنْ يَحْصُلَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ وَاشْتَغَلَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَايَةُ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالنِّهَايَةُ فِي الشَّفَقَةِ وَالْمَرْحَمَةِ عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ عَلَى رَجَاءٍ مِنْهُ أَنْ يُصِيبَ مَنْ أُسْنِدَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْحُكُومَةُ الْحَقَّ وَيَظْفَرَ بِالثَّوَابِ فَيَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْبُلُوغُ إِلَى مَا جُعِلَتْ لَهُ الْحُرُوبُ عَلَى الْمُسَالَمَةِ وَالْمُصَالَحَةِ اقْتِدَاءً بِمَا أَمَرَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَصْبِ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي الِاخْتِلَافِ بَيْنَ الزَّوْجَيْنِ وَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي اخْتِلَافٍ وَقَعَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ وَمَا جَرَى مِنَ الِاصْطِلَاحِ فَالْأُمَّةُ الَّتِي جَاءَتْ فِيهِمُ الشَّهَادَةُ عَنِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِالْآخِرَةِ وَأَمْرُ الدِّينِ الَّذِي عَظُمَ أَمْرُهُ التَّدَبُّرُ وَالنَّظَرُ وَالْإِمَامَةُ الَّتِي الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهَا التَّأْلِيفُ وَالْأَمْنُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ يُعْمَلَ لَهَا ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ هَؤُلَاءِ لَمَّا أَقَرُّوا بِالْإِمَامَةِ وَالْخِلَافَةِ وَعَلِمُوا بِالْأَسْبَابِ الَّتِي ظَهَرَتْ لَهُمْ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ مِمَّا صَلَحَ بِهَا لِلْخِلَافَةِ ثُمَّ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَغَيَّرَتْ تِلْكَ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَبَدَّلَتْ ثُمَّ كَانَ التَّحْكِيمُ مِنْهُ حُكْمًا حَكَمَ بِهِ بِسَبَبِ الْإِمَامَةِ فَيَلْزَمُهُمْ بِحَقِّ إِمَامَتِهِ الْقَبُولُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ ضَاقَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَجْهُ مَعْرِفَةِ عُذْرِهِ فِي ذَلِكَ ثُمَّ الْعَجَبُ مِنْ غَبَاوَةِ الْخَوَارِجِ أَنَّهُمْ خَطَّأُوهُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا ذَلِكَ حُجَّةً لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ فِيمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَبْلُ إِذْ كَيْفَ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالْمُصَالَحَةِ ثُمَّ كَانَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْحُرُوبِ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ مِنْ أَنْ جَعَلُوا الْأَمْرَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنَ الْحُرُوبِ دَلَالَةً عَلَى خَطَئِهِ فِي الثَّانِي وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ فَاحِشَةٌ وَتَعَلُّقُهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي مُسْتَقِيمٌ لِأَنَّهُ ذُكِرَ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا وَنَحْنُ كَذَا نَقُولُ إِنَّ الِاشْتِغَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ أَوَّلًا بِالدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الصُّلْحِ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِ الْيَأْسِ عَنِ الصُّلْحِ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْقِتَالِ لِيَحْصُلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِذَلِكَ وَهُوَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ وَاجْتِمَاعُ الْكَلِمَةِ وَاللَّهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ.
He brought together their hearts, but Allah brought them together, and He said: 'And you became, by His favor, brothers' the verse. He brought them together. So when unification exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what he knows of the weariness of the two parties and what appears of the effects of seeking rest from them and attaining security, wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the evil of fighting and to unite hearts and unify the word. So Ali, when he witnessed the effects of weariness among the people, hoped that unification of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he engaged in it, and it is the ultimate goal of wisdom and the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah, in hope that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted might attain the truth and gain reward. In that is the attainment of what wars are intended for: peace and reconciliation, following what Allah Almighty commanded in appointing two arbiters in dispute between spouses, and what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed two arbiters in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what took place of reconciliation. So the ummah, about whom testimony from Allah Almighty concerning the Hereafter came, and the matter of religion whose importance is deliberation and consideration, and the imamate whose purpose is unification and security, is more deserving that this be done for them. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his (Ali's) self that made him fit for the caliphate, and then those reasons did not change in him nor alter, and then the arbitration from him was a ruling he made due to the imamate, then it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that was narrow for them. Then the wonder is at the stupidity of the Khawarij that they considered him mistaken in the arbitration. Had they made that an argument against him concerning what happened before—why did he not begin with reconciliation and then resort to war?—that would be closer than their making the first matter of war an indication of his error in the second. This is gross ignorance. And their clinging to His statement: 'Then fight the one that transgresses' is valid, because it was mentioned after His statement: 'Then make peace between them.' And we likewise say: engagement should first be with invitation to peace, then after despair of peace, one returns to fighting to achieve the desired goal thereby, which is unification of hearts and unity of word. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1182

Commentary
This passage is a sustained defense of Ali's decision to accept arbitration (tahkim) at Siffin, refuting the Khawarij's charge that it was a sinful error. The author begins by citing Quranic verses showing that Allah can bring hearts together without war, establishing that peace is preferable. He then explains that Ali, seeing war-weariness, sought unification through arbitration as an act of wisdom and mercy. He draws parallels to Quranic arbitration between spouses and the Prophet's arbitration at Hudaybiyya. The author then argues that since the Khawarij accepted Ali's imamate, they must accept his judgment even if they don't fully understand his reasoning. He criticizes their inconsistency: they condemn arbitration but earlier accepted Ali's warfare. Finally, he clarifies the correct understanding of the Quranic command to fight the transgressor: it comes after the command to make peace, so priority is to invite to peace, and only when that fails to fight. The entire passage is structured as a systematic refutation of the Khawarij's position.

Key Terms
الإمامة
الخوارج
التحكيم
الصّلح
القتال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khawarij thought that the Quranic command to fight the transgressor (Quran 49:9) implies immediate war without prior peace efforts.
Correction: The author points out that the verse is preceded by a command to make peace, so peace must be attempted first.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against the Khawarij's claim that Ali erred in arbitration?
A) The Khawarij never really accepted Ali's imamate.
B) The Khawarij should have criticized him for not seeking peace first, but instead they criticized him for seeking peace after war.
C) The Khawarij misinterpreted the Quranic verse about fighting.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Obedience to the imam requires accepting his judgment, and the Quranic order is peace first, then fighting only as a last resort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever insisted on a critical opinion about a leader's decision while ignoring your own limited knowledge? This lesson demands you consider: can you accept authority even when the reasoning is obscure? What would it cost you to withhold judgment and submit?
?
When you use a Quranic verse to justify a position, do you first check its full context and the sequence of commands? How often have you, like the Khawarij, used a proof-text without considering what precedes it? What change will you make today in how you approach scripture?
?
The author says the Khawarij's criticism was 'gross ignorance' because they were inconsistent. Where in your life are you inconsistent—criticizing someone's later action while ignoring the earlier ones that contradict your critique? Will you humbly reexamine your own logic today?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
8 min
The Khawarij's Dilemma: Dialogue vs. Fighting
Nasafi poses a four-branch dilemma refuting the Khawarij's inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses a dialectical dilemma to prove the Khawarij logically condemn themselves whether they admit error or not.

Core Idea
The Khawarij's own logic traps them in inevitable self-contradiction.

The Khawarij insisted that anyone who accepted arbitration after the Battle of Siffin was a disbeliever, yet they themselves engaged in dialogue with Ali and Ibn Abbas while delaying fighting. Imam al-Nasafi exposes this inconsistency through a simple but powerful dilemma. By following the four possible answers the Khawarij could give, you will see that each one forces them to admit either disbelief or error—the very charge they leveled against others.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. The first sentence poses the question: do the Khawarij become disbelievers by debating Ali and Ibn Abbas while postponing fighting?
2
Trace the four possible answers
Identify each branch: (1) They say yes, they become disbelievers. (2) They say no, then ask if they were mistaken or correct. (3) If mistaken, they admit error = disbelief. (4) If correct, then Ali's delay by arbitration is also correct.
The argument forces a concession regardless of their response.
3
Understand the analogy to Ali
Notice how the last branch draws a direct parallel: if the Khawarij delayed fighting hoping for return to truth, then Ali did the same through arbitration. Consistency demands they accept Ali's correctness.
This refutes their core accusation against Ali.
4
Historical note: Ali's own argument
The passage mentions that Ali himself used this exact reasoning, leading many Khawarij to repent. Reflect on the power of this logical approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُنَاقَشَةُ الْخَوَارِجِ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ
وَيُقَالُ لِلْخَوَارِجِ: إِذَا اشْتَغَلْتُمْ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا وَدَعَوْتُمُوهُمَا إِلَى مَا اعْتَقَدْتُمْ وَتَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُمَا فِي تِلْكَ الْمُدَّةِ رَجَاءَ أَنْ يَعُودَا إِلَى رَأْيِكُمْ أَكْفَرْتُمْ بِذَلِكَ أَمْ لَا؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: نَعَمْ فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِالْكُفْرِ، وَإِنْ قَالُوا: لَا. قِيلَ: أَفَكُنْتُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ مُخْطِئِينَ أَمْ مُصِيبِينَ؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُخْطِئِينَ. فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِالْخَطَأِ وَهُوَ كُفْرٌ عِنْدَهُمْ، وَإِنْ قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُصِيبِينَ. قِيلَ: وَلِمَ كُنْتُمْ كَذَلِكَ وَقَدْ تَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ مُدَّةَ مُنَاظَرَتِكُمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُوَ كَافِرٌ فَكَذَلِكَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يَصِيرُ كَافِرًا بِتَرْكِهِ مُقَاتَلَةَ أُولَئِكَ؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: إِنَّا تَرَكْنَا قِتَالَنَا رَجَاءَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَهُوَ رُجُوعُهُ إِلَى الْحَقِّ بِدُونِ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْمُقَاتَلَةِ. قِيلَ: فَكَذَا عَلِيٌّ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ اشْتَغَلَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ لِهَذَا، وَحُكِيَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا احْتَجَّ عَلَيْهِمْ بِهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ سَبَبَ رُجُوعِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْهُمْ عَنْ ضَلَالَتِهِ. مَا يَحْكُونَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا شَكَّ فِي نَفْسِهِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَصِفْهَا بِإِمْرَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَجَابَهُمْ وَقْتَ التَّحْكِيمِ إِلَى أَنْ لَا يُكْتَبَ عَلَى أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. كَلَامٌ فَاسِدٌ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَشُكَّ فِي ذَلِكَ بَلْ أَرَادَ بِذَلِكَ حَسْمَ الشَّغَبِ، وَقَدْ فَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ
Discussion of the Khawarij concerning their statement about the arbitration. It is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in debating Ibn Abbas and then after that in debating Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) and invited them to what you believed, and you abandoned fighting them during that period hoping that they would return to your opinion, do you thereby become disbelievers or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted against themselves disbelief. If they say: No. It is said: Then were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken. They have admitted against themselves error, which is disbelief according to them. If they say: We were correct. It is said: Why were you so, when you abandoned fighting him during the period of your debating him while he was a disbeliever? So likewise, Ali does not become a disbeliever by abandoning fighting those people. If they say: We abandoned our fighting hoping for the attainment of the goal, which is his return to the truth without the need for fighting. It is said: So too Ali, except that he engaged in arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued against them with this very same point, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance. What they narrate that Ali doubted in himself when he did not describe himself as Commander of the Faithful and agreed with them at the time of arbitration not to write 'Commander of the Faithful' – this is corrupt speech. For he did not doubt in that, but rather intended by that to cut off discord. And the Messenger of Allah indeed did...
Source pages p. 1183

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical refutation of the Khawarij. It first poses a dilemma: if the Khawarij engaged in dialogue with Ibn Abbas and Ali while suspending fighting, they either become disbelievers or not. If they say yes, they admit their own disbelief. If no, then they must be either correct or mistaken. If mistaken, that is disbelief by their own standard. If correct, then they delayed fighting for hope of return to truth, which is exactly what Ali did when he accepted arbitration for the same reason—so Ali is also correct. The author adds that Ali himself used this argument, leading many Khawarij to repent. Then he addresses the claim that Ali doubted his own title by agreeing to drop 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document. He dismisses this as corrupt speech, explaining that Ali did not doubt but aimed to cut off discord, and cites an incomplete prophetic precedent (likely the treaty of Hudaybiyya where the Prophet agreed to drop his title).

Key Terms
مُنَاظَرَة
التحكيم
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Khawarij's stance was logically consistent because they only rejected arbitration, not dialogue.
Correction: The dilemma shows that their own practice of dialogue while delaying fighting is indistinguishable from arbitration in its intent, leading to self-condemnation.

Checkpoint
According to the dilemma, if the Khawarij answer that they were correct in debating Ali while delaying fighting, what conclusion follows?
A) They admit disbelief.
B) They admit error.
C) They must accept that Ali's arbitration is also correct.
D) They must resume fighting immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij's own actions logically force them either to admit disbelief or to accept Ali's arbitration as correct, refuting their core accusation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you condemn others for something you yourself practice? How does the Khawarij's dilemma expose your own double standards? Write one step you will take today to align your judgments with consistency.
?
The Khawarij thought they were sincere in their fight for truth, but their logic trapped them. What deeply held conviction of yours might be undermined by your own actions? Are you willing to examine it with the same rigorous logic this passage applies?
?
If you were in the place of the Khawarij, would you have the humility to accept that your own standard condemns you when you debated Ibn Abbas? When was the last time you admitted that your own argument turned against you? What would it take for you to repent like those who returned from misguidance?

Ali's Alleged Doubt: The Title of Commander
Nasafi refutes the claim that Ali doubted his imamate by dropping his title.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Khawarij's claim that Ali doubted his own imamate by dropping his title at arbitration.

Core Idea
Ali's removal of his title was a tactical move to end discord, not a sign of doubt.

The Khawarij also argued that Ali's agreement to drop the phrase 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document proved he doubted his own legitimacy. Imam al-Nasafi dismisses this as corrupt speech, explaining that Ali's intention was to cut off discord, following the precedent of the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Hudaybiyya. This lesson examines that rebuttal and its basis in prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the Khawarij claim
The Khawarij claimed that Ali doubted himself because he did not insist on the title 'Commander of the Faithful' in the arbitration agreement.
2
Understand the refutation
The author states this is corrupt speech (كَلَامٌ فَاسِدٌ). Ali did not doubt; he aimed to cut off discord (حَسْمَ الشَّغَبِ).
3
Connect to prophetic precedent
The passage begins to cite the Prophet's action (likely the Treaty of Hudaybiyya where he agreed to remove his title). Reflect on how this parallel validates Ali's decision.
The text cuts off, but the reference is clear to those familiar with the seerah.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this refutation protects the integrity of Ali's leadership and highlights the Khawarij's superficial reading of events.

مُنَاقَشَةُ الْخَوَارِجِ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ
وَيُقَالُ لِلْخَوَارِجِ: إِذَا اشْتَغَلْتُمْ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا وَدَعَوْتُمُوهُمَا إِلَى مَا اعْتَقَدْتُمْ وَتَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُمَا فِي تِلْكَ الْمُدَّةِ رَجَاءَ أَنْ يَعُودَا إِلَى رَأْيِكُمْ أَكْفَرْتُمْ بِذَلِكَ أَمْ لَا؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: نَعَمْ فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِالْكُفْرِ، وَإِنْ قَالُوا: لَا. قِيلَ: أَفَكُنْتُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ مُخْطِئِينَ أَمْ مُصِيبِينَ؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُخْطِئِينَ. فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ بِالْخَطَأِ وَهُوَ كُفْرٌ عِنْدَهُمْ، وَإِنْ قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُصِيبِينَ. قِيلَ: وَلِمَ كُنْتُمْ كَذَلِكَ وَقَدْ تَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ مُدَّةَ مُنَاظَرَتِكُمْ إِيَّاهُ وَهُوَ كَافِرٌ فَكَذَلِكَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يَصِيرُ كَافِرًا بِتَرْكِهِ مُقَاتَلَةَ أُولَئِكَ؟ فَإِنْ قَالُوا: إِنَّا تَرَكْنَا قِتَالَنَا رَجَاءَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَهُوَ رُجُوعُهُ إِلَى الْحَقِّ بِدُونِ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْمُقَاتَلَةِ. قِيلَ: فَكَذَا عَلِيٌّ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ اشْتَغَلَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ لِهَذَا، وَحُكِيَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا احْتَجَّ عَلَيْهِمْ بِهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ سَبَبَ رُجُوعِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْهُمْ عَنْ ضَلَالَتِهِ. مَا يَحْكُونَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا شَكَّ فِي نَفْسِهِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَصِفْهَا بِإِمْرَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَجَابَهُمْ وَقْتَ التَّحْكِيمِ إِلَى أَنْ لَا يُكْتَبَ عَلَى أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. كَلَامٌ فَاسِدٌ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَشُكَّ فِي ذَلِكَ بَلْ أَرَادَ بِذَلِكَ حَسْمَ الشَّغَبِ، وَقَدْ فَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ
Discussion of the Khawarij concerning their statement about the arbitration. It is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in debating Ibn Abbas and then after that in debating Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) and invited them to what you believed, and you abandoned fighting them during that period hoping that they would return to your opinion, do you thereby become disbelievers or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted against themselves disbelief. If they say: No. It is said: Then were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken. They have admitted against themselves error, which is disbelief according to them. If they say: We were correct. It is said: Why were you so, when you abandoned fighting him during the period of your debating him while he was a disbeliever? So likewise, Ali does not become a disbeliever by abandoning fighting those people. If they say: We abandoned our fighting hoping for the attainment of the goal, which is his return to the truth without the need for fighting. It is said: So too Ali, except that he engaged in arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued against them with this very same point, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance. What they narrate that Ali doubted in himself when he did not describe himself as Commander of the Faithful and agreed with them at the time of arbitration not to write 'Commander of the Faithful' – this is corrupt speech. For he did not doubt in that, but rather intended by that to cut off discord. And the Messenger of Allah indeed did...
Source pages p. 1183

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical refutation of the Khawarij. It first poses a dilemma: if the Khawarij engaged in dialogue with Ibn Abbas and Ali while suspending fighting, they either become disbelievers or not. If they say yes, they admit their own disbelief. If no, then they must be either correct or mistaken. If mistaken, that is disbelief by their own standard. If correct, then they delayed fighting for hope of return to truth, which is exactly what Ali did when he accepted arbitration for the same reason—so Ali is also correct. The author adds that Ali himself used this argument, leading many Khawarij to repent. Then he addresses the claim that Ali doubted his own title by agreeing to drop 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document. He dismisses this as corrupt speech, explaining that Ali did not doubt but aimed to cut off discord, and cites an incomplete prophetic precedent (likely the treaty of Hudaybiyya where the Prophet agreed to drop his title).

Key Terms
إِمْرَة الْمُؤْمِنِينَ
حَسْمُ الشَّغَب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khawarij believed that Ali's removal of his title meant he doubted his own right to rule.
Correction: The passage clarifies that it was a strategic decision to end discord, not a reflection of doubt.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Ali agree not to write 'Commander of the Faithful' in the arbitration document?
A) He doubted his imamate.
B) He wanted to cut off discord.
C) He was forced by the Khawarij.
D) He changed his mind about his role.

Key Takeaway
Ali's removal of his title was a wise tactic to end discord, following the Prophet's example, not a sign of doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a situation where you insisted on a personal title, recognition, or status even though it caused friction or division. What would Ali’s example of dropping his title for the sake of unity challenge you to do differently this week? Name one concrete action you can take.
?
Have you ever judged someone’s faith or sincerity based on a single external action, without understanding their true intention? How does the lesson’s warning against 'corrupt speech' and its call to look at the deeper objective (cutting off discord) change your approach to judging others?
?
Ali followed the Prophet’s example by prioritizing peace over personal status. Are you willing to sacrifice your own reputation or pride to bring people together? What is holding you back from taking that step today?

Refutation of the Khawarij on Arbitration
The author refutes the Khawarij by turning their own argument against them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Khawarij by exposing an inconsistency in their own actions regarding fighting and arbitration.

Core Idea
The Khawarij's own delay in fighting disproves their objection to Ali's arbitration.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of the Khawarij's stance on arbitration (tahkīm). The author constructs a dilemma based on the Khawarij's own behavior: they delayed fighting Ibn Abbas and Ali while debating them, yet they condemned Ali for delaying fighting through arbitration. By turning their argument against them, the author reveals a self-contradiction that led many Khawarij to abandon their error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice the dialectical structure: the author poses a series of questions to the Khawarij.
2
Identify the dilemma
The argument hinges on a dilemma: either the Khawarij committed disbelief by delaying fighting, or they were correct. Trace each horn and its consequences.
The author forces them into a contradiction regardless of their answer.
3
See how the Khawarij's defense is turned against them
The Khawarij claim they delayed fighting hoping for the opponent's return to truth. The author points out that Ali's arbitration had the same intention.
This equalizes their situations, refuting their objection.
4
Reflect on the historical outcome
Note that Ali himself used this argument, causing many Khawarij to repent. This shows the effectiveness of the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقال للخوارج: إذا اشتغلتم بمناظرة ابن عباس ثم بعد ذلك بمناظرة علي - رضي الله عنهما - ودعوتهما إلى ما اعتقدتم، وتركتم قتاله في تلك المدة رجاء أن يعود إلى رأيكم أكفرتم بذلك أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: نعم فقد أقروا على أنفسهم بالكفر، وإن قالوا: لا. قيل : أفكنتم في ذلك مخطئين أم مصيبين؟ فإن قالوا: كنا مخطئين. فقد أقروا على أنفسهم بالخطأ وهو كفر عندهم، وإن قالوا: كنا مصيبين. قيل : ولم كنتم كذلك وقد تركتم قتاله مدة مناظرتكم إياه وهو كافر فكذلك علي لا يصير كافرًا بتركه مقاتلة أولئك؟ فإن قالوا : إنا تركنا قتالنا رجاء حصول المقصود وهو رجوعه إلى الحق بدون الحاجة إلى المقاتلة. قيل: فكذا علي إلا أنه اشتغل بالتحكيم لهذا ، وحكي أن عليا احتج عليهم بهذا بعينه، فكان ذلك سبب رجوع كثير منهم عن ضلالته.
And it is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in debate with Ibn Abbas and then with Ali - may Allah be pleased with them both - and called them to what you believed, and left off fighting them during that period hoping that he would return to your opinion, did you thereby commit disbelief or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted to disbelief against themselves. And if they say: No, it is said: Were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken, then they have admitted to error against themselves, and error according to them is disbelief. And if they say: We were correct, it is said: Then why were you so, while you left off fighting him for the duration of your debate with him, considering him a disbeliever? So likewise, Ali does not become a disbeliever by leaving off fighting those people. If they say: We left off our fighting hoping to achieve the objective, that is, his return to the truth without need for fighting. It is said: So too with Ali, except that he engaged in arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued against them with this very point, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance.
Source pages p. 1183

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Khawarij concerning their stance on arbitration (tahkīm). The author constructs a dilemma: he asks the Khawarij whether their own delay in fighting Ibn Abbas and Ali—while they debated them in hopes of convincing them—constituted disbelief (kufr) or not. If they say yes, they admit to kufr; if no, they are asked whether they were correct or mistaken in that delay. If they say mistaken, then by their own standard, error is kufr. If they say correct, the author points out the inconsistency: they delayed fighting someone they considered a disbeliever, so why should Ali be considered a disbeliever for delaying to fight them while he pursued arbitration? The Khawarij's likely response is that they delayed hoping for the opponent's return to the truth without fighting. The author then turns this against them: Ali's arbitration was done with the same intention. He concludes by noting that Ali himself used this argument, leading many Khawarij to abandon their error.

Key Terms
